[Dn 2:4b- 7:28; Ezr 4:8–6:18, 7:12, 7:26; Je 10:11; Gn 31:47aB.]

NOTE.- In the case of words common to Biblical Aramaic and Biblical Hebrew the etymological matter already given with the Hebrew words is not repeated here. The sign + is prefixed to all words peculiar to the Biblical Aramaic. In other cases, except where Targum or Syr. is mentioned alone, it may be understood that the words occur also in the Aramaic of the Targums and in Syriac, even when this is not expressly stated.

1090: w>, W conj. and (BH w>), used mostly as in Heb., except that there is no w ‘consecutive’;—and, connecting both words (Dn 2:5) and sentences (ib.). When three or more words are connected together, w> may connect them all (Dn 2:6, 2:10, 4:34, 5:18), or only the two last (2:17, 3:4, 4:4, Ezr 6:9), or the three last (Dn 2:37 3:21), or be omitted altogether (2:27, 5:11, cf. 3:2, Ezr 4:9). w> also connects vbs., in cases where BH would use •w:, as Dn 4:2, 5:29, 6:17, 6:25; in such cases a Pf. is oft. followed by a Ptcp., as Dn 2:7 !yrim.a('w>An[}, so v:10, 3:9, 3:16, 3:24 +, hence in 2:5, 2:8, 2:15, 2:20 and often read prob. with Nö:GGA 1884, 1021 rm;a'w> hn"[} (for hnE['). Dn 2:16, 2:18); and also Dn 6:29; = with, 7:1. b. connecting contrasted ideas, but Dn 2:6, 3:6, 3:18, 4:4. c. = and so, Dn 2:49, 6:2, esp. after imv. 2:4, 2:9, 2:24, or impf. 2:7. d. to express an intention Dn 5:2 !ATv.yIw> that they might drink: after a command, etc., even with ptcp. or perf., nearly = that, 2:13, 6:2 (cf.
